Land Bureau; Urges Payment of Assessment Fees; Deadline Extended to the End of August and No Further Extension Will Be Granted 131

The Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau issued a notice yesterday, stating that the cases of submitting applications for increasing land rent and specially requesting the increase of land on the Bund have been notified to pay the assessment fee, but those who have delayed payment were previously notified to be limited to June 30 of this year. Those who exceed the deadline should have their original cases cancelled. Now that the deadline has passed, there are still those who have not complied with the payment. The Bureau has repeatedly given deadlines for payment, and has given three orders and five requests, but they are still watching and not paying as before. The original cases should have been cancelled in accordance with the previously announced clearing method, and the land should be taken back into municipal ownership, so as to avoid the accumulation of more and more pending cases and hinder the reorganization. However, in order to give extra consideration, another extension is specially granted until August 31 of this year. All households that have been notified to pay the fee for land according to the ministry and request to increase the land on the Bund before the date of the notice must pay the assessment fee that should be paid according to the original notice within the deadline to the Bureau, so as to issue a certificate and close the case. If the payment is not made again after the deadline, the original cases will be cancelled separately, and personnel will be sent to draw public land maps based on the actual land measured, and send them to the Finance Bureau for safekeeping and disposal. Those who have adjacent original private land and are included in the map will be drawn separately, and maps and certificates will be made and notified to be collected. No further extension will be granted, and no matter what reason is given, it will be invalid. In addition to reporting to the Municipal Government, it is urgent to announce it for everyone to know, so as not to make a mistake. This notice is hereby issued, signed by Deputy Director Xu Fu.

Pitiable Coolie; Died of Illness in a Tile Tube; Corpse Rotting and Foul Odor Emanating 132

An anonymous coolie man, about 40 years old, died of illness in a cement tile tube placed by the Municipal Bureau on an open space on Route Massenet in the French Concession because he had no place to sleep at night. No one found out, causing the corpse to swell and rot, and a foul odor emanated. It was not until 6:00 pm on the 25th that a Chinese patrolman No. 148 from the Lujiawan Central Police Station smelled a pungent odor while patrolling, and then discovered it. People could not get close to it. He immediately reported to the Central Police Station, which sent a detective to investigate. The corpse seemed to have been dead for many days, and it was unbearably foul. He immediately notified the Tongren Fuyuan Branch to send laborers to hoist the corpse into the mortuary, first put it in a coffin, and report to the Special Second Court Prosecutor's Office today for inspection.

Chinese Commercial Securities Exchange Holds Annual General Meeting of Shareholders Yesterday, Reports on Business Conditions, Distributes Shareholder Dividends 134

(Shen Bao Special Dispatch) The Chinese Commercial Securities Exchange held its sixth annual general meeting of shareholders at its market on Hankou Road yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. 173 shareholders attended, representing 31,427 shares. In addition to reporting on the sixth operating period continuing from the end of June of the 25th year, resolutions were passed regarding the distribution of dividends. Details of each matter are recorded as follows:

Chairman's Report After the customary formalities, the chairman of the exchange, Zhang Weiru, first gave a report stating that approximately 173 shareholders, representing 31,427 shares, were present at this annual meeting. The exchange's business previously encompassed more than ten types of government bonds and securities. Since the reorganization by the Ministry of Finance, there are now only five types of government bonds, including the Unified and Revival Bonds. This has severely impacted the business. Therefore, the agricultural trade market was temporarily closed for three weeks, requesting relief from the Ministry of Finance. Subsequently, the exchange implemented strict austerity measures and reduced expenditures, and business gradually improved. As a result, the dividend for this period is still more than two yuan per share, which is something to report with relief to the shareholders. If the exchange continues with this austerity policy, I firmly believe that it will gradually expand in the future.

Business Conditions Subsequently, Standing Director Yin Yunsheng reported on business conditions, stating that after the closing of accounts at the end of December of the 24th year, until the end of June of the 25th year, which was the end of the sixth operating period of continuing business, the operating assets were still calculated separately. The total surplus under operating items was 220,459.07 national currency, and the surplus under asset items was 148,932.63 national currency, totaling 369,391.70 national currency. After allocating various items according to the articles of association, a proposal for the distribution amount is respectfully submitted for the shareholders' meeting to deliberate and implement. Regarding the business situation of this period, the total revenue from handling fees in six months was 475,703.59 national currency, averaging slightly more than 2,964 national currency per day. Expenditures for operating expenses in six months totaled 255,479.68 national currency, averaging slightly more than 1,419 national currency per day. Various assets are still depreciated according to the old rules. Now, in accordance with Article 37 of the articles of association, various schedules have been compiled and are respectfully submitted for your review. Subsequently, Supervisor Kong Songxin reported on the accounting, (omitted).

Dividend Distribution Soon after, the proposed profit distribution determined by the directors was submitted for discussion. The exchange's operating surplus for this period was 220,459.07 national currency. First, 10.5% was allocated for business tax, totaling 22,248.20 national currency, which was added to the asset surplus of 148,932.63 national currency, totaling 347,143.50 national currency. 69,428.70 national currency was allocated for this period's reserve fund, and 7,584 national currency was used to replenish the previous reserve fund. After allocating shareholder dividends and employee bonuses in accordance with the regulations, it is proposed to distribute a dividend of 2.50 yuan per share for this period. The shortfall of 2,908.44 yuan will be allocated from the retained earnings of the previous period, and the remainder will still be classified as retained earnings. This was approved by resolution. At 2:30 PM, the meeting was adjourned.

Minutes of the Shanghai Silk Industry Bank's Extraordinary General Meeting of Shareholders 138

The Shanghai Silk Industry Bank, located at 460 Hankou Road, previously decided by the board of directors to convene an extraordinary general meeting of shareholders on July 26 (i.e., yesterday) at 4:00 PM on the fourth floor of the bank. The meeting was attended by over 290 shareholders, including Chen Aishi, Feng Zhong, Pei Yunqing, Ye Yinshan, Zhu Wenqi, Shen Jisi, Lu Baoguang, Lu Zhengbing, Ma Shaoquan, Ge Shuqian, Shen Qinqi, Wang Boying, He Wuliang, Cai Shengbai, Zheng Zenan, Xu Xinliu, Yu Zuoting, Sun He, Fu Ruihe, Xu Shengyang, Chen Qingzhao, Chen Ziming, Wu Yun Chu, Cao Ziyu, Liu Zhan'an, etc., holding a total of 4,999 shares and 3,607 proxy votes. Luo Qinghua was elected as the temporary chairman. After the customary formalities, the chairman rose to report, stating briefly: "Since the establishment of this bank, it has been during the aftermath of the January 28th Incident. Industry and commerce were in decline, and finances were exhausted, making progress particularly difficult. Fortunately, thanks to the support of the shareholders and the assistance of various sectors, the amount of deposits has increased daily over the past four years, and various businesses have also been promoted in order. It has successively joined the Banking Association and the Joint Reserve Committee's Clearing House as a member and was the first to promote commercial acceptance drafts, which has been well received by society. It has also established branches and warehouses in various silk regions such as Hangzhou, Shaoxing, Beijing, and Shengze to provide various types of loans, greatly benefiting the silk industry. Its reputation has also increased as a result. However, the state of global economic downturn has deepened daily. In the past two years, due to the instability of the financial turmoil and the continuous intrusion of rumors, the difficulties encountered by this bank are conceivable. Last winter, in order to expand business and relieve the silk industry, this bank had requested Chairman Chiang to instruct the Ministry of Finance to make proper arrangements to replenish the bank's capital. This spring, after the Ministry of Finance sent personnel to investigate the bank's contents, it repeatedly ordered the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Bank of Jiangsu to handle the matter. After repeated consultations between the directors and supervisors of this bank and the authorities of the three banks, it is now recalled that the Bank of Jiangsu has agreed to provide substantive assistance, with the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications serving as a backing, providing funds at low interest rates to fully expand its business. On the one hand, Chairman Wang of this bank requested the board of directors to pass a resolution to hire Mr. Lu Zidong, General Manager of the Bank of Jiangsu, to concurrently serve as the General Manager of this bank, in order to receive substantive assistance and thorough rectification. The newly appointed General Manager Lu has already arrived at the bank on the 16th of this month to take up his post and has discussed concrete measures for improving business, which are being promoted in order. Various deposits have begun to return, and the total amount of deposits has increased daily, indicating that after this bank has strengthened its financial resources and established its direction, its credit is becoming more solid, and its future is bright. Colleagues will continue to work hard and strive to live up to the trust placed in them by the shareholders. It is hoped that you will not hesitate to provide guidance and assistance." Next, the chairman read the board of directors' reports and requested their approval. As a result of the discussion, they were unanimously approved. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

Longhua Temple Monk Sued for Issuing Bad Checks, The monks were each fined 30 yuan. 148

Longhua Temple has been in poor shape recently and is often burdened by lawsuits. Half a month ago, the temple's deputy abbot Hong Kui was sued in the District Court by the temple's hill owner Lu Mingzhao for sodomizing a believer, Yang Shouchang. The investigation was clear, and Hong Kui was detained and sentenced to three years and two months of imprisonment. One wave has not subsided, and another wave rises. The reason is that the temple owed 320 yuan to the Ruitai Electrical Appliance Store on Lujiabang Road for installing electric lights the year before last. After repeated demands for payment, they issued a check in April this year, which was from Jincheng Bank. Unexpectedly, when they went to cash the check at maturity, it was a blank, unrooted item. Therefore, the store owner Tao Junxian sued the temple in the District Court for issuing bad checks. The defendants were the abbot monk Xingkong, the manager monk Yongchan, and the deputy abbot Hong Kui (the one who was sentenced to three years and two months). After Judge Lu examined and interrogated them the other day, he ruled that the three defendants had issued bad checks and fined them each 30 yuan, with incidental civil litigation, requesting them to apply to the civil court themselves.

Tanziawan Wannian Nunnery: Two Nuns Fight Over Abbess Position; One Claims to Have Resolved Lawsuit by Paying to Leave the Country; the Other Claims Unwillingness to Accept the Situation and Illegally Occupies the Nunnery's Property 149

In Zhabei Tanziawan, there is a nunnery named Wannian Nunnery, currently presided over by an elderly nun named Zijian. It has over ten acres of land, over ten rooms, and over ten young nuns. Their daily life is relatively comfortable. Unexpectedly, yesterday at around 2 PM, multiple cars suddenly arrived, carrying about twenty men and women who escorted a nun inside to take over the abbess position. Nun Zijian, without any prior notice, felt as if a bolt from the blue had struck, with someone forcibly seizing her position. Therefore, she and the other nuns firmly resisted, leading to a dispute. However, the newcomers were numerous, and they were quickly outnumbered. So, they secretly reported to the Tanziawan police station, which sent officers to investigate. Upon seeing the police arrive, the twenty or so men and women who had escorted the nun got back into the cars and sped away, leaving only the nun named Xiujing at the nunnery. After questioning by the police, both Zijian and Xiujing were taken to the police station. According to Zijian, she is seventy years old, from Suzhou, and resides in Wannian Nunnery in Tanziawan. Xiujing was formerly her disciple but was expelled. They had a lawsuit that was resolved by paying one thousand yuan to leave the country, and there is evidence of this. Today, she is returning to fight for the abbess position, which is impossible, and so on. Xiujing stated that she is fifty-one years old, from Hangzhou, and currently resides at 127 Gongxing Road. From 1925 to 1930, she was the abbess. Later, a nun named Zhonglin managed the nunnery. Unexpectedly, Zhonglin suddenly died, and Zijian did not notify her, but instead illegally occupied the nunnery's property, refusing to return it to her, and so on. After verifying the statements, the interrogating officer immediately submitted them to the new sub-bureau for resolution.

Hengfeng Road Police Chief and Residents of Shantytowns Accuse Each Other; Court Awaits Resolution of Shantytown Residents' Lawsuit Before Summoning and Hearing the Police Chief's Accusation 150

Lu Pei, the police chief of the Hengfeng Road Police Station in Shanghai, is the younger brother of former detective captain Lu Ying. He has held the position since 1934. Recently, representatives Peng Yuanfeng, Miao Xiangben, and Liu Zhaocai, representing over a thousand Jiangbei shantytown residents, filed a lawsuit in the Shanghai District Court accusing him of dereliction of duty and harming the people. According to them, the shacks are built on land owned by Gu Lanji, who does not interfere. However, Lu Pei repeatedly evicts them, falsely claiming requests from the landowner. When the landowner was questioned, they all denied it. The shantytown residents have suffered from the destruction of their homes and are greatly disturbed. On March 7th, the shacks near Changan Road caught fire twice. The case was heard in criminal court, but only the shantytown representatives appeared. The interrogation was not concluded. Now, Police Chief Lu Pei has accused Peng Yuanfeng, Miao Xiangben, Liu Zhaocai, and others of slander in the District Court Prosecutor's Office. Prosecutor Li Fen held a hearing the day before yesterday, and both Lu and Peng attended. After reviewing the case, the interrogating officer stated that because the lawsuit filed by Peng and others has not yet been resolved, the hearing will be postponed.

First Quarter of This Year 153

— The Egg Industry in Shanghai, Edited by

(Part 33 of the Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce)

(1) Overview: Eggs are a byproduct of farming and are produced throughout the country. They can be used for food and as raw materials for industry. As early as the early years of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, fresh eggs were shipped to Japan. In 1901, crude egg factories were first established in the Chinese mainland to manufacture egg yolks and egg whites, which were sold to export merchants and then shipped to Europe and the United States. In 1914, an American company established the Banda Egg Factory in Shanghai, at which time it had switched to mechanized frozen eggs. During the European War, sales were brisk and developed year after year. 1929 was the industry's heyday, ranking third among exported goods. In recent years, trade has been somewhat less vibrant, with a tendency to decline. This is due to the weak purchasing power of various countries and the pressure of exclusion. Chinese merchants have gradually improved the quality, and there are no defects to speak of. The United Kingdom is the largest purchaser of Chinese eggs. Of the 32,094,662 yuan of exports in 1935, the United Kingdom purchased 18,480,314 yuan, accounting for 57 percent. Therefore, how to maintain Sino-British egg trade has become the focus of discussion in the industry. Shanghai is an important market for eggs, with six frozen egg factories, one crude egg factory, thirteen crude egg factory branches in Shanghai, more than ten export merchants, and no fewer than fifty small-scale egg shops. Only Maochang Company is a Chinese-owned frozen egg factory, but the company is a leader in the egg industry, with annual sales accounting for about one-fifth of the country's total exports, which is a source of comfort for Chinese merchants.

(2) Production Areas and Sources: According to the seventh agricultural and commercial statistics of the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce before 1922, there were 147,648,746 chickens in the country, producing 4,489,703,425 eggs, and 52,249,322 ducks, producing 1,035,194,130 eggs. These figures seem too old and can only be used as a general reference. In recent years, due to banditry and floods in various places, coupled with the decline of the rural economy and the bankruptcy of farmers, egg production has been hit hard. At the same time, distant provinces and counties still have transportation difficulties. Even if there is a surplus, it is not easy to export. This is what we should pay attention to.

Shanghai is an industrial and commercial area, and the egg production in the surrounding countryside is very limited. Its sources are roughly divided into four locations: 1. The southern section of the Jinpu Railway, such as Gangshan, Suzhou, Guzhen, Bengbu, Yingzhou, Zhengyangguan, Shouzhou, Mingguang, Haozhou, Luzhou, Puzhen, and Hexian; 2. The Yangtze River route, such as Jiujiang, Anqing, Datong, and Wuhu; 3. The Jiangbei route, such as Guanyun, Huaiyin, Baoying, Yancheng, Taixian, Jiangdu, Gaoyou, Dongtai, Xinghua, Rugao, and Nantong; 4. The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo route, such as Quzhou, Lanxi, Jinhua, Zhuji, Xiaoshan, Hangxian, Chongde, Jiaxing, and Pinghu, with the first and third routes being the most active. Crude egg products must be made into dry products before they can be transported to Shanghai. The Jiangbei route is also the most abundant source, as crude egg factories are concentrated in Jiangsu and Anhui.

Transportation of egg-producing areas relies mainly on railways, followed by ships. In order to encourage exports, the Ministry of Railways reduced freight rates for egg products starting from May 11, 1934. Fresh eggs were reclassified and charged at the fourth-class freight rate, dried or powdered egg yolks in boxes were reclassified as third-class freight, wet egg yolks in barrels were reclassified as fourth-class freight, dried or powdered egg whites in boxes were reclassified as third-class freight, and eggs in barrels were reclassified as fourth-class freight. Eggs coming to Shanghai from Jiangbei are packed in containers holding approximately 600 to 750 eggs each, while those from the Jinpu Railway hold approximately 800 eggs each. The weight is between 75 and 80 catties. Currently, light weight is preferred to prevent breakage. The total miscellaneous expenses per hundred catties amount to about three yuan for fast routes and two yuan for short routes.

(3) Types of Eggs: Eggs are composed of carbon, oxygen, hydrogen, nitrogen, sulfur, and other substances, making them nutritious. For thousands of years, China has only used them for food and did not know their various uses. Since the rise of crude egg factories, we have learned to emulate Europe and the United States, separating the substance into egg yolks and egg whites to make various egg products. The types of egg whites are described below:

1. Fresh Eggs: The raw material for all egg products. If they are to be transported elsewhere, they must first undergo egg candling to distinguish their quality. After candling, they are packed in wooden boxes. Each small box can hold 360 eggs. The temperature of the boxed fresh eggs must not exceed 22 degrees Fahrenheit.

2. Egg Products: There are various types of dried whole eggs, dried whole egg powder, dried whole egg slices, flying whole eggs, flying egg yolks, flying egg yolk powder, dried egg yolks, and light egg yolks. Egg yolks are made with chemicals and can be divided into two types: one made with boric acid and one made with sodium benzoate. Light egg yolks are also made with boric acid, but the salt is removed. Most of the above products without salt are used as food, while those with salt are mostly used as raw materials in industry. Egg yolks are used for tanning leather, and egg whites are mostly used for food.

3. Frozen Eggs: Invented in the United States, this is the most complete and refined method of production. The product is packed in specially made tin cans, with each can ranging from 5.5 to 44 pounds. It is stored in cold storage. When transported, it is transported in refrigerated barges, and when exported, it is stored in refrigerated holds, which can be stored for a long time without spoiling. Also known as frozen eggs, this is currently the largest seller of eggs.

4. Century Eggs: Table salt, lime, red ash, , golden gong bottom, tea, and other ingredients are mixed together with appropriate amounts of water, and then fresh duck eggs are immersed in them. After about one to two weeks, they are ready. Those produced in Beijing are the most famous.

5. Salted Eggs: Salt and ash or clay are mixed with water and applied to the outer layer of the eggshell. They are ready after about a month. Those produced in the Jiangbei area are the most well-known.

The conversion ratio of egg products to raw eggs is as follows:

Frozen Eggs: 120 pounds equal

to 1,120 eggs

Egg Yolks: 120 pounds equal

to 5,600 eggs

Dried Eggs: 120 pounds equal

to 4,500 eggs (To be continued)

Sports News

A Record of the National Games Team's Journey (Third Letter) by Special Correspondent Feng Youzhen from the Central News Agency 154

(10)(7) Singapore Miscellany

Yesterday, I hastily wrote a little about the situation in Singapore at the public banquet of the Singapore Overseas Chinese community. Now the mail ship has passed through the Strait of Malacca and is heading towards Colombo, Ceylon, in the Indian Ocean. There are still many things to report about Singapore, and I will extract them as follows. Singapore is the gateway to the Malay Peninsula and a hub for commerce and transportation. It is located on the coast where the South China Sea and the Indian Ocean meet, making it a strategic passage for Euro-Asian transportation. Its position is very important. Although Britain's aggression in Asia is based primarily on Hong Kong, its headquarters are in Singapore.

The British have a governor who manages the Malay Peninsula. The governor's office is located in Singapore. They rule the entire island with a very small number of British people and do not reveal any weaknesses at all.

According to a survey three years ago, the total population of Singapore is 540,000, of which 420,000 are overseas Chinese. On July 1 of this year, the government conducted another census. The results have not yet been published, but the number of overseas Chinese has probably not decreased.

Most of these 400,000-plus overseas Chinese are engaged in commerce. The shops we see on the streets are almost all opened by overseas Chinese. In the past, people in China thought that doing business in the South Seas Islands was like digging for gold, a shortcut to wealth. However, in recent years, the trend of depression has swept the globe, and the South Seas are no exception. The business of overseas Chinese has also been declining. In addition, the dumping policies of Japan are advancing rapidly in the South Seas. Taking Singapore as an example, there are only 10,000 Japanese people, but they occupy a large part of the commercial power, which greatly threatens our overseas Chinese who are accustomed to living in peace. However, on the whole, the business of overseas Chinese can still be sustained.

Overseas Chinese education has been developing rapidly in recent years. There are now hundreds of elementary schools and six middle schools, all teaching in Mandarin. Most of the overseas Chinese are from Fujian and Guangdong. In the past, in addition to the Fujian and Guangdong dialects, they could at most understand English and the Malay dialect. Mandarin was almost unusable. In recent years, as a result of promoting education, the young overseas Chinese can all speak Mandarin. The textbooks in the schools are all shipped from China, but textbooks that involve imperialism are prohibited from being used. Imperialists want to maintain the security of their colonies, so this measure is expected. Overseas Chinese are more concerned about the situation in their motherland than their compatriots in China. Living overseas, they are subjected to oppression and trampling, and they pray every day that their country will become stronger and stronger. We should not neglect overseas propaganda. The municipal administration of Singapore is very well-managed. The streets are clean, the buildings are tidy, and there is lush greenery everywhere. It is simply a park-like city. In terms of public security, the governor's office maintains a very peaceful and tranquil environment with very few military and police forces. This is very noteworthy. Transportation is very developed. Not only is the city of Singapore flat and wide, but the roads throughout the Malay Peninsula, even in remote rural areas, are also accessible in all directions. In addition to connecting the important cities of the entire island, the railway also runs directly to Siam.

Most of the Malay natives are farmers, and their main products are rubber, coconuts, jackfruit, and pineapples. Coconut trees can be seen everywhere, and many are planted even on the sidewalks of the roads. The tall trunks, palm-like leaves, and large fruits adorn the unique tropical flavor. Tin is the main mineral product and occupies a very important position in the world.

(10)(8) The News Industry in Singapore

The news industry in Singapore is very developed. There are four English newspapers, two Japanese newspapers, and five Chinese newspapers. The five Chinese newspapers are (1) Sin Chew Jit Poh, (2) Sing Chong Jit Poh, both of which were founded with investment from the wealthy overseas Chinese businessman Hu Wenhu, (3) Nanyang Siang Pau, founded with investment from the wealthy businessman Chen Jiageng, (4) The New Citizen Daily, which is a party newspaper and has the longest history, and (5) Zonghui Xinbao, originally a royalist organ newspaper, is now a commercial newspaper. Except for Sin Chew Jit Poh, which publishes a special evening edition at 5:00 PM every day, the rest are morning editions, published at 6:00 AM every day. Except for The New Citizen Daily, which has five large sheets, the rest have six large sheets. Sin Chew Jit Poh has the largest circulation, with more than 11,000 copies. Zonghui Xinbao has the smallest circulation, with 3,000 copies. Sin Chew Jit Poh, Sing Chong Jit Poh, and Nanyang Siang Pau are all equipped with rotary presses, which makes printing very fast. The business of each newspaper cannot be balanced by revenue and expenditure and must be maintained by subsidies.

Although the layout and editing methods of each newspaper cannot be compared with those of the major newspapers in China, and there is much room for improvement, their dedication and tension at work are truly amazing and admirable. The overseas Chinese are very concerned about the situation in the motherland. Several major newspapers have special telegrams sent from Shanghai and Hong Kong. The special telegrams that arrive at 4:00 AM every morning can be published in the morning edition that is published at 6:00 AM. On the day we arrived in Singapore, the newspapers reported the news of our Chinese delegation in great detail. Because I was sending letters and telegrams, I went to visit Sin Chew Jit Poh. All the staff were very excited and busy preparing for the evening edition. The photos taken at the public banquet at 2:00 PM were developed and plated at 3:00 PM. The basketball game only ended at 4:30 PM, but the results were published in the two-page evening edition at 5:00 PM. As for the situation of the whole delegation arriving in port, it was even more detailed. This kind of hard work and amazing results is probably rarely matched by the major newspapers in China.

The biggest difficulty in running a newspaper in Singapore is that the government's interference is too great and there is no freedom of speech. It is said that although the Governor's Office does not check news and speeches before the newspaper is published, the penalties are very severe if there are any errors they deem to be made after publication, and they are deported at any time. Up to now, fifteen of our compatriots have been deported back to China for running newspapers in Singapore. Therefore, the responsibility of the newspaper editor is very heavy. In general, what the Singapore government fears most is attacking, criticizing, and inciting words. Whether intentionally or unintentionally, touching their taboos is considered unforgivable. Student Group

Tang Baojia, a student from Shanghai University, lost to Kerasha in the first week of the open singles with scores of 6-4, 2-6, 5-7. His forehand and backhand strokes are excellent, his net play is also commendable, and his court positioning is quite clever. It is a pity that his serve is slightly lacking. Li Guofan, from Yenching University in Beiping, plans to apply to Shanghai Jiaotong University. His forehand stroke is his specialty, and his serve is heavy and powerful, making for a beautiful performance. However, after each hard hit, he is extraordinarily negligent in preparing for the return, and when the opponent returns with a heavy ball, he is instead unable to cope. This is his only weakness, and this negligence in crucial shots seems to have become a habit, resulting from an inability to concentrate. His skills are not inferior to those of Tang. Both are outstanding young talents in the tennis world with promising futures.

The match began with Tang Baojia serving. After a 2-1 game, Li Guofan took the lead with 3-2. After 3-3, Li Guofan won three consecutive games to win the first set 6-3. Tang Baojia gradually improved, often shooting low, fast balls into the corners of the opponent's service area, and sometimes shooting deep balls towards both sides of the baseline, allowing him to lead 4-1. After Li won a game, he lost his own service game, and in the next game, he repeatedly touched the net or hit the ball out of bounds. Tang Baojia then won back a set 6-2.

The third set was the final set, and the competition was extremely fierce. Li Guofan once held an extremely advantageous position at 5-3. Tang Baojia calmly fought back, winning back Li's service game and winning his own service game with a slip, tying the score at 5-5. Li then took the lead again at 6-5, and Tang won another clean game to make it 6-6. Continuing to 7-6, Tang took the lead. In the next game, Tang also lost a clean game, making it 7-7 again. After that, Tang repeatedly scored first in a game, while Li equalized. After 10-10, Tang finally took two consecutive games and won the final victory. Both players performed well, earning praise from the audience.

In this match, there is another noteworthy event. Not long after the match began, Tang Baojia's racket suddenly broke. He temporarily borrowed the racket of his opponent in the final, Li Guofan. As a result, Li lost to Tang. Li Baojun jokingly said, "Tang Baojia borrowed a knife to kill someone." Someone else said, "Is this also 'using the Chinese to defeat the Chinese'?"

Ministry of Education Revises Elementary School Regulations (1) 165

The Ministry of Education has now announced the revised elementary school regulations. This revision of the elementary school regulations is based on the results of research opinions from education authorities in various provinces and cities and the experience of elementary school implementation in recent years. Detailed sorting has been carried out, and articles on the appointment, treatment, and protection of elementary school teachers have been added, reducing overlap with other regulations. The main points of the revision and the full text of the revision are recorded below:

Points of Regulation Revision

(1) Regarding the elementary school academic year, semester, and holiday dates, there are already provisions in the Ministry of Education's promulgated regulations on the revision of the school academic year, semester, and holiday dates. The old regulations listed it as a chapter, and this chapter has now been deleted and changed to an article listed in Chapter 1, General Provisions. (2) Regarding short-term elementary schools, the Ministry of Education has separately formulated temporary regulations for one-year short-term elementary schools and has abolished the first phase of implementation, implementation methods for compulsory education, and implementation methods for short-term compulsory education. This article has now been revised appropriately, and methods for simplified elementary schools are stipulated, to be formulated by the education administrative organs of each province and city and submitted to the Ministry of Posts and Communications for record. (3) The period for provincial elementary schools and affiliated elementary schools of national colleges and universities to report children's rosters to the local county and city education administrative organs has been changed to within one month after the start of each semester. (4) Hygiene expenses have been added to the allocation of elementary school operating expenses. (5) The elementary school teaching subjects and weekly teaching hours, based on the revisions promulgated in February 1936, are listed. (6) Local township teaching materials may be edited by the competent education administrative organs, as well as by the schools. (7) The period for elementary schools to accept transfer students in each grade, originally three months after the start of each semester, has now been changed to two months after the start of each semester. (8) The regulations on "assistant teachers" in elementary school teachers and staff have been deleted, and it is stipulated that the number of teachers per two grades should be three in principle. (9) All articles regarding the examination of elementary school teachers have been deleted, as the Ministry of Education has separately formulated temporary regulations for the examination of elementary school teachers. (10) Elementary school teachers who have elementary school teacher qualifications or have passed the elementary school teacher examination are now required to apply to the competent education administrative organs for registration. Elementary schools should hire teachers only after registration and announcement, except in special circumstances. (11) The daily time for elementary school teachers and staff to be at school has now been changed to eight hours, and the teaching time has been reduced to a maximum of 240 minutes. (12) Elementary school teachers who have been dismissed without cause are allowed to present reasons and request the competent education administrative organs to investigate and correct the situation. (13) The appointment, treatment, and protection of kindergarten principals and teachers shall be subject to the regulations on elementary school teachers and staff. (14) It is stipulated that elementary school teachers and staff shall not be promoted or demoted with the change of principals or competent education administrative personnel.

Full Text of the Revised Regulations

Chapter 1 General Provisions

Article 1 These regulations are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 17 of the Elementary School Law.

Article 2 Elementary schools are the places where national compulsory education is implemented, and their implementation guidelines are based on the provisions of Article 1 of the Elementary School Law. Article 3 Elementary schools shall accept school-age children aged six to twelve, with a study period of six years.

Article 4 For the sake of promoting compulsory education, simplified elementary schools and short-term elementary schools may also be established in various places. The methods for simplified elementary schools shall be formulated by the education administrative organs of each province and city and submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval and record. Short-term elementary schools shall be handled in accordance with the Ministry of Education's regulations for short-term elementary schools.

Article 5 The elementary school academic year, semester, and holiday dates shall be handled in accordance with the provisions of the revised regulations on school academic year, semester, and holiday dates.

Chapter 2 Establishment and Management

Article 6 In order to promote the establishment of elementary schools and facilitate management, each county and city should divide school districts in accordance with the revised methods for dividing elementary school districts in cities and counties.

Article 7 The elementary schools attached to normal schools and colleges above the vocational level that train teachers shall have the same nature as single-set elementary schools, except that they are used for the practice of normal school students.

Article 8 Elementary schools established by provinces and cities or colleges above the vocational level that train teachers for educational experiments shall be called "Experimental Elementary School of..."

Article 9 Provincial elementary schools shall be named after the place where they are located. Public elementary schools below the county and city level shall be named after the smaller area. When there are two or more public elementary schools with the same name in one place, they may be distinguished by the order of numbers. Private elementary schools should use a specific name and should not use the name of a place as the school name. (To be continued)

Ministry of Education Orders Elementary Schools to Abolish Corporal Punishment 166

(Nanjing, 26th) In order to abolish corporal punishment and harsh punishment in elementary schools, the Ministry of Education has ordered the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities to instruct local elementary school teacher research associations to conduct separate research. The research results reported to the Ministry include those from fourteen provinces and cities, including Hunan, Hubei, Shandong, Shanxi, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, Henan, Shaanxi, Beiping, Tianjin, Qingdao, and Nanjing, as well as the Weihaiwei Management Office and the Experimental School of Central University. They believe that all corporal punishment that punishes children and causes physical pain, or harsh punishment that is indeed harmful to children's bodies, should be abolished. The Ministry has handed it over to the National Children's Annual Conference for sorting and will print it into a booklet for distribution throughout the country in order to effectively promote abolition.

Spring and Autumn

Snippets 169

— (Hua Jia)

There are many different views on destiny. And apart from some energetic young people, many people believe that humans are controlled by the god of destiny, especially those who are older or middle-aged and have a lot of experience. The reason is that they have more experience, more setbacks, and their vigor has been lost with their age, so they feel utterly disappointed. The reason for defending themselves that arises from this negative outlook on life is that the god of destiny controls them—if luck is bad, any effort is in vain.

Their reasons seem very reasonable on the surface, but sometimes after thinking carefully, they are all nonsense. The fact is often the most eloquent, and a person's efforts often overcome their destiny. Otherwise, there would be no evolution from ancient times to the present, and there would be no human history, because if everyone used destiny as an excuse not to work hard, wouldn't humans be inferior to animals?

The great musician Beethoven once said: "I want to fight destiny to the death, it will not completely conquer me." This sentence is very valuable. No matter how powerful destiny is, if we fight it to the death and try desperately, it will not completely conquer us. Recently, the reason why China has declined is that some people are unwilling to work hard, and seem to be waiting for death. I wonder what they think after reading Beethoven's words?

Mr. Hu Zhantang's Elegant Hobbies 170

— Divine Eagle

—Lotus Leaf Rice: Red Waist Rice—

Party and state elder Mr. Hu Zhantang passed away some time ago. There have been many reports in the north and south about anecdotes about the former Mr. Hu. The "Lotus Rice" and "Red Waist Rice" matters recorded in this article have not been mentioned by anyone, so it may be helpful to record them briefly.

In his later years, Mr. Zhantang was weak and ill, so he was extremely careful about his diet and daily life. During the summer and autumn seasons, he would abstain from meat and eat vegetarian food all day long. Even for important social engagements, he would only choose light and refreshing dishes to eat a little. In the summer of the year before last, while avoiding the heat in Hainan, he dined with Zou Haibin, Xiao Focheng, and others in the Pearl River Villa. Most of the dishes were fatty, so Mr. Hu dared not touch them. As the meal was about to end, a dish called "Lotus Leaf Rice" was brought to the table by a waiter, with a clear fragrance overflowing. Haibin smiled and said to Mr. Hu that lotus leaf rice is a famous product of Dongguan and is made entirely with vegetarian ingredients. Why doesn't sir try it? Mr. Hu nodded and chewed it slightly. Not only was it extremely delicious, but it was also fragrant and refreshing, not dry or greasy. It was truly a wonderful product for the summer season. Mr. Hu ate one-fourth of it, more than a large bowl, that day, and praised it endlessly after eating. His daughter, Gongzi Mulan, discussed it with the chef Song Silang after the banquet and hired him as a permanent chef. From then on, the "Lotus Leaf Rice" of Dongguan became famous far and wide. Many dignitaries in Guangdong often visited the private residence in Dongshan to enjoy it. After entering Mr. Hu's residence, Song also suggested to Mr. Hu's family to buy "Red Waist Rice," a specialty of Dongguan, to cook porridge for Mr. Hu, which was also sweet and delicious. The rice grains are longer than Bijeng rice, and there is a red line around the waist. The porridge is pink in color and is a refreshing and nourishing product. Unfortunately, Dongguan's production is not high, and it cannot be planted elsewhere due to soil conditions, so people in various provinces and cities can only hear its name but cannot taste its deliciousness.

The Night at Touji Bridge 171

— Wei Jing

The mystery of the night, in Shanghai, used to be praised on North Sichuan Road. After January 28th, it shifted to Avenue Joffre in the French Concession. However, the low-level mystery of the night developed from the streets east of the Great World and the original Six-Ma Road and Four-Ma Road area, northward to Touji Bridge, and then westward, spreading to North Nicheng Bridge and the Jiangyuan Lane area. This is perhaps something that those who like to talk about Shanghai anecdotes should consider a feeling of vicissitude?

After dinner, heading north from Risheng Building, young women dressed in red and green cheongsams, powdered and jade-like, stand outside the shop windows, waiting to be courted. At the intersections of the side streets, groups of two or three are waiting, forming an orderly skirmish line. If you brush past them and glance at them, they will respond with a charming smile. If at this moment, the pedestrian slows down a bit, heh heh heh, they will secretly tell you the price of true ecstasy, and add a sentence "It's cheap!" At the same time, within this cheap price, there is still room for you to bargain by 30 or 20 percent. This scene is being played out everywhere in an area formed by the four points of Risheng Building, Touji Bridge, Nicheng Bridge, and North Nicheng Bridge. It is performed under the ghostly red light. After midnight, the eastern end of Xinzha Road is even more lined up in anticipation, almost completely occupying the sidewalks on both sides. Every prostitute's face is filled with lascivious smiles, teasing the pedestrians. Here, apart from vagrants, there is no sign of men insulting women. All there is, is the embarrassed plight of men being insulted, scurrying away. Sometimes, you can even see a comical scene of a man being half-pulled and half-dragged by several prostitutes, being pushed towards a mysterious den.

Hygienists say that in such a setting, the air is filled with the most disgusting atmosphere. If our glasses had the effect of a microscope, we could definitely stare blankly and see countless venereal disease germs moving in the air. This may be an exaggeration, but when we see the thriving practices of those venereal disease doctors, we should be able to understand the working efficiency of these mysterious women, right?

How terrifying, these evil spirits of venereal disease germs!

Swapped Phoenixes 172

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Four: Sight and Sound are Not Illusions, Hesitant to Resume Business; Life and Death Can Be Entrusted to a Generous and Strange Elegy

But studying these words from beginning to end, he concluded that they were very pitiful. A woman. If she uses polite words to address someone, she definitely does not treat them as a casual acquaintance. Thinking this way, it doesn't seem like one can say that she is deliberately rejecting him, right? He put the letter on the table, pressed it with a copper ruler, then put his hands behind his back and paced back and forth in the room. Sometimes he stood in the middle of the room, raised his head and looked at the sky. Sometimes he held his right elbow with his left hand, and rested his cheek on his right hand, and looked down at the ground. When he wasn't spacing out, he put his hands behind his back again and walked back and forth in the room. The old lady sat in the main room wearing a pair of large glasses, holding a piece of old clothing in her hands, sewing it in a desultory manner. Hearing the sound of footsteps constantly echoing from the study, she stopped her needlework, held the clothes in her arms, and looked towards the room, saying: "Guoqi, what is bothering you so much today that you are so restless?" Guoqi exclaimed "Oh," only then did he wake up, immediately stopped, and smiled at Granny Zhang: "You old lady, you treat me like a three-year-old child. If I walk a few more steps in the room, you become worried." Granny Zhang said: "It's not that I'm worried. You have been different recently. You are always fine, but then you start spinning around in the room, inside and out. In the past, when you were thinking about writing, you would sometimes pace back and forth in the room like this. But it wouldn't take long before you would settle down. It's not like recently, there's always something weighing on your mind that you can't let go of. What is it that's bothering you? Just tell me." As she said this, she simply took off her glasses with both hands, put them in her lap, and looked at Guoqi with even more concern. Guoqi smiled: "I definitely don't have anything on my mind. Even if I do, it's just about writing. How could I trouble you to share my worries?" Granny Zhang said: "If that's really the case, then I won't ask. But from what I see, you don't seem to be thinking about writing." Guoqi walked into the main room, intending to cover it up, but when he saw his mother's kind face, all the words he had prepared in his heart were held back. He smiled slightly and said: "A friend wrote me a letter, and I want to reply, but it's very difficult to find the right words." Granny Zhang said: "That's very common, why make such a fuss? What did he write to you about?" Guoqi shrugged his shoulders twice before smiling slightly and saying: "It's an irrelevant matter." Granny Zhang said: "If it's an irrelevant matter, why do you keep dwelling on it?"

Special Feature

Gaoqiao Sea Bathing 173

— Ge Chonglou

I live in Shanghai, but I have never enjoyed the taste of a "sea bath." So this Sunday, I went to the most luxurious "sea bathing beach."

The sunlight shone on the bronze man at the bronze man's pier. The bronze man did not sweat like people do. The bronze man is not afraid of the hot summer.

Houfei and I, and our two bicycles, took the Shanghai ferry from the Bund at 10:30 AM.

The boat carried people in the yellow river. The wind was strong, and the waves splashed on people's faces. People were like standing in the uncovered rain.

"Look at those red-dressed country girls, those oily green wild trees, those yellow farming cattle, those carefree chickens and dogs." I pointed out the scenery on both banks to Houfei.

Houfei nodded. He is also a member who is tired of urban life. The ship stopped several times and arrived at Gaoqiao at noon. Gaoqiao Wharf is still several miles away from the beach. We have bicycles to use as transportation.

Our cars passed through the fields, and the seedlings in the fields were all yellow! Southern women were dancing with agricultural tools. Seeing such a scene, it reminds people of the poem "Hoeing millet under the midday sun, sweat drips onto the soil; who knows that the food on our plate? Every grain is hard-earned!"

Before long, we arrived at the "Seaside Bathing Beach." We first bought tickets at the entrance, changed our clothes in the changing room (into swimsuits), and ran to the beach.

The scene before us unfolded. In the distance, the water and the sky were connected. Some tourists who arrived earlier than us were squirming in the water like ants. We walked barefoot on the sandy beach, leaving our footprints one by one on the sand. Walking forward, we reached the muddy ground. The mud was knee-deep, which was somewhat like the situation of farmers transplanting rice seedlings.

The water gradually deepened! We stopped at the place where ships came and went (because there was no water mark, it would be dangerous if it was deeper). We started swimming in the warm water under the sunlight: breaststroke, backstroke, freestyle... Houfei and I shouted excitedly, but this shout was drowned out by the sound of the waves!

People are like a small boat floating on a giant stream. People's hearts feel light. The waves even more diligently wash away the dirt on people's bodies, as if receiving a great baptism.

The tide came! The huge waves rolled and tumbled. We all returned to the shore. The sand and mud that were exposed when we came were now all submerged by the tide.

We rested on the shore for a while, ate some Gaoqiao specialty pastries, and then embarked on our journey home. Lightly fluttering butterflies followed our wheels, as if to see us off.

Although this trip was only a small circle, I felt quite satisfied in my heart!

Small Spring and Autumn Weekly

Above and Below 174

— (Jin Boying)

In the despotic era under the emperor system in the past, the words "above" and "below" were often used to distinguish the noble and lowly classes of the governed and the rulers. Like Mencius said: "'Above' and 'below' compete for profit. 'Above' has no moral standards. 'Below' has no laws to abide by."

Nowadays, general writers and scholars also write: "The whole country is united 'above' and 'below'." "The government and the public 'above' and 'below'." I don't know what "above" and "below" refers to?

"Above" without a tile to stand on. "Below" without an awl to stand. These "above" and "below" are all included in our poor scholars. It can be said that we live in an equal position.

"Above" goes to heaven. "Below" goes to hell. Symbolizing the disparity between joy and suffering in the world. These two words "above" and "below" show that there is a world of difference.

Chengdu Anecdotes 175

— Jiong

A friend returned from Chengdu, telling me about the customs of Chengdu, so I recorded a few things:

Chengdu produces a lot of red beans (also known as acacia beans), which the locals call "rouge beans." They also call it "Western red beans," and there is a market price, selling for 1,000 cash per tael (equivalent to only five cents in Shanghai). There are more than thirty beans. People in that area have no interest in them. According to the record, red beans are produced in extremely small quantities, and people cherish them. There are two red bean trees on Mr. Qian Muqi's manor in Furong Village, Changshu, which have not borne fruit for several years. But the production of red beans in Chengdu has not been recorded, which is very incomprehensible.

The kitchen of Qingyang Palace in Chengdu is made of Phoebe zhennan wood. Phoebe zhennan wood has always been a precious wood. It is actually used to build a kitchen, which shows the abundance of Phoebe zhennan wood in Chengdu.

Chengdu has a kind of single-wheeled cart, which can only carry one person. The locals call it "chicken cart." It is said that it is "wooden ox and flowing horse."

The rice pot of Zhaojue Temple in Chengdu has a diameter of one zhang. There are four in total, which can feed 3,000 people. It is really rare.

In recent years, I have discovered that there are a few words that have a very mysterious meaning when used alone in a sentence. Although it can be understood tacitly, it is not easy to explain. Now I will record them below:

The "suo" character in "obtained a son with one 'suo'."

The "ran" character in "had an affair with ××."

The two characters "yun yu" in "secretly started cloud and rain."

A Method to Resolve Jealousy 177

— Lan Shan

A certain gentleman had one wife and one concubine, and they were endlessly jealous of each other. The gentleman was helpless, so he went to an antique shop and bought two jade monkeys, secretly giving one to his wife and one to his concubine, without either of them knowing. He instructed them both, "Don't let anyone other than the two of us know about this, hide it well." Both the wife and the concubine obeyed and treasured them without fail. One day, the wife and the concubine both asked the gentleman, "Who do you love most between the two of us?" The gentleman said sadly, "Whoever has my jade monkey between the two of you is the one I love the most." Neither the wife nor the concubine said anything, but they were secretly delighted in their hearts, thinking that only they were loved by their husband, and the other party did not have this favor. Their jealousy then ceased. That gentleman can truly be called an expert in deceiving women. Those who have two females in the family, please pay attention.

Common Sense for Taking Long-Distance Buses 178

— Xianweisheng

According to experienced travelers, because the road surface of long-distance buses is uneven, the bumps are very severe. For passengers, the best seat is one behind the driver, like "first class." The opposite seat is second best, like "second class." The others are in order, the further back the worse!

Hanging from the Collar 179

— Linghu Zhao

A certain military officer saw a young man by the riverbank, hanging from a willow branch, still moving. The military officer asked in surprise: "Friend, what are you doing?"

"! Hanging!" The young man rolled his eyes.

"Oh, you're wrong. You should tighten the rope around your neck. You're only hanging from your collar now!" The military officer said.

"Yes. I originally put the rope around my neck, but I could barely breathe, so I had to change my approach!"

Contradictory Words 180

— (Ma Tinglong)

A nation that claims to be prosperous can often eat Siamese rice and foreign wheat.

Why do lawyers who are well-versed in the law often end up in court due to disputes over concubines?

While vigorously promoting the New Life Movement and eradicating superstition, why do people often hold welcome-the-gods festivals at the same time?

Although the market is sluggish and the economy is tight, why do theaters and dance halls still often hang "full house" signs?
