Economic Special Issue

A Re-examination of China's Currency Problems 181

— Wu Xiaofu

Almost everyone will agree that there is still a need to re-examine China's currency problems, and that there is a need to improve China's currency facilities. However, whatever new facilities and improvements China's currency may have in the future, it seems appropriate to discuss here the main content and causes of China's currency problems up to the present!

As everyone knows, China's currency problem is closely related to all other disputes in China; China's currency problem is a constituent cause of China's entire economic, political, and social problems, and at the same time a product of all these problems. Therefore, it cannot be regarded as pointless moaning to propose such a currency problem for a renewed and abstract analysis. The task of this article is not to make a complete and abstract analysis of this problem, but only to provide a brief explanation of certain aspects.

1. The content and causes of China's currency problem: Does it refer to the currency system problem? Or what? Perhaps the general public thinks that our currency problem is merely a currency system problem. This is insufficient. Our currency problem actually mainly includes two aspects: the relation of currency and their mutual influence.

We now want to look at our currency problems from a vertical perspective first.

Those who study China's currency problems all know, or should know, that the entire currency history of China for thousands of years is full of currency problems, and has never obtained much profound solution (in the narrow sense, the rest follows this).

Our monetary history is divided into two major parts by the great powers. The first part is the period before the intrusion of foreign powers, i.e., before 1842. The second part is the summer period after the intrusion of foreign powers. The period from 1842 to the present belongs to this period. The intrusion of the great powers divided China's economy, politics, culture, etc. into two parts that could not be connected in the slightest, but only produced extremely terrible conflicts, contradictions, and disorders in the distance of one hundred and eight thousand miles and in the vortex of one hundred and eight thousand miles—these are two completely different and increasingly disparate periods. This period division dissected China alive. And who was dissected? It is the Chinese masses who have suffered and are suffering unspeakable pain!

It is so in all aspects, why not in currency? Before the intrusion of the great powers, China was always trapped in the stagnant and cyclical feudal small-peasant economy and the quagmire of commercial capital. In this quagmire, the feudal economy sometimes declined (the period from the end of the Han Dynasty to the Sui Dynasty was a major period of decline - Note 1), and sometimes revived (the Tang Dynasty was like this - Note 2). With the rise and fall of the feudal economy, China's currency situation showed a posture of stability and development from time to time, and disorder and decline from time to time - and in the general trend, just like China's economic situation, China's currency was extremely backward. Yes, China's currency is adapted to China's economy (this is the case in every country under normal circumstances), and from the end of the Han Dynasty to the Sui Dynasty, it was very declining and chaotic; the currency of the Tang Dynasty was relatively stable and developed. (These are all examples to illustrate). And from the Zhou Dynasty to the end of the Qing Dynasty, for more than 3,000 years, China only used copper, with copper as the main currency, and what was used was still very small cash. From Emperor Wu of the Han Dynasty to the end of the Sui Dynasty, the famous Wushu coins ruled intermittently for 735 years. From Emperor Gaozu of the Tang Dynasty to the end of the Qing Dynasty (let's take the end of the Qing Dynasty as an example), Tongbao coins generally maintained their authority for 1,293 years. The fact that a very small cash can rule for such a long time also shows how backward China's economy and currency were in the past. And even today, the Chinese masses still use copper as the main currency, and there are still cases of using cash in remote areas (such as Minqin, Dingxin, and Yongchang counties in Gansu Province - Note 3).

When the foreign forces invaded, China was still pitiful and ridiculous (but the rulers at that time felt extremely arrogant) and used its "Celestial Empire" cash greatly. At that time, the basic currency was out of the question, and the currency standard was only used in practice as the copper standard. Although silver was also used, silver was only in the position of non-coin auxiliary currency.

It was under such circumstances that the great powers broke through the Great Wall!

Before the intrusion of the great powers, China's economy was backward and exchanges were undeveloped, so its currency was also extremely backward. After the great powers intruded, they transformed China's economy with their own capitalist models (what kind of transformation did they make!). This caused China's economy to drastically commoditize. So, did China's economy and currency have a prosperous development from then on? Not at all. The great powers only fully utilized the backward historical conditions of China's economy and currency, etc., to make China continue to lag behind, make China its appendage, its tail, and its outer government. The great powers only used and are still using various general and special means to oppress China's national industry, bind and manipulate China's national currency capital, so that all of this cannot make any development contrary to the interests of the great powers.

Needless to say, the cannons and commodities of the great powers, even in terms of currency, also imported various foreign silver dollars, and even foreign silver dollars specifically for aggression against China (the United States cast trade dollars Trade pillar to import into China) to extract our wealth. In addition, they also established banks in China and issued banknotes, attempting to directly rule China with foreign currencies. After the intrusion of the great powers, the various feudal chaos and separatism in China's currency reached an alarming degree. This indicates and reflects the fact that the great powers are supporting China's feudal forces in order to sell their plan to enslave China.

Precisely because of the direct and indirect (the so-called indirect refers to the great powers supporting China's feudal forces, the rest follows this) invasion and oppression of the great powers, China's currency has not been able to develop normally, and has been suffering from silver. Moreover, the silver standard system, which was established as late as 1933, was suddenly abandoned by China on October 15, 1934. The late arrival and hurried departure of China's silver standard system is another wonderful symbol of the backwardness and crisis of China's economy and currency, etc.

In terms of currency capital, all of China's currency capital accumulated through simple plunder, commercial capital, usury, etc., except for the vast majority that has been pocketed by the great powers, the remaining small amount is, as shown above, bound and manipulated by the great powers, and is directly and indirectly kept in the mud of usury, various speculative undertakings, and commercial capital as much as possible, so that it cannot be used for undertakings that are contrary to the interests of the great powers. (Currently, bank investment has changed somewhat in direction, but it is still very far from the central industry). As a result, China's currency capital, which cannot obtain normal economic development due to the seizure of the market and the lack of economic development, is unable to invest in the central industry, so our industry and economy are even more affected, and this result aggravates the morbid state and crisis of the currency, making it even more impossible for the currency to obtain normal economic development. If currency capital cannot be developed, how can the currency system be improved alone? And the various direct and indirect blows given to us by the American silver policy are even more "kicking a man when he's down" and "adding insult to injury."

In this way, the severity of China's currency problem today is the result of the direct and indirect invasion and oppression of the great powers from the economic and political aspects. Under the oppression, China has no way to develop economically, and even falls into an increasingly dangerous situation, and its currency naturally has no way to develop and stabilize. The crisis in China's currency today is the same as the danger in the economy. The biggest source of the crisis is political, not economic, special (such as smuggling), not general.

2. The Basic Tone of the Solution to China's Currency Problem

Before talking about the basic tone of the solution to China's currency problem, we still need to talk a few words about the particularity of China's currency problem. Some of the peculiarities of China's currency, such as feudal chaos and separatism, are more obvious, so I won't talk much about them here. However, what needs to be pointed out is that the extremely (relatively speaking) backward historical conditions of China's currency and the deformed state caused by the combination of the rule of foreign financial capital are a major feature. And the fact that China has sunk so deeply into the pain and suffering of silver is also a major feature.

In the current state, everyone feels that it is necessary to improve our currency system, everyone feels that it is necessary to liberate our currency capital, and everyone feels that it is necessary to make our currency develop normally economically. However, talking about improvement under the increasingly pressing direct and indirect infringement of the great powers is indeed not an easy task. The gold standard, the silver standard, the gold exchange standard, etc., all have their problems to varying degrees. So, should we fundamentally abandon currency to solve the currency problem? Can we adopt methods such as "property certificates"? That's even more problematic. This is very important and very interesting, let's talk a few more words about it by the way.

Some people, seeing that the social economy is so difficult and that the national financial problem is becoming increasingly serious, want to indulge in fantasy and think that they can fundamentally abolish currency, this "disaster," to get rid of their troubles. Yes, even from the perspective of financial problems, it is imperative to seek improvement in currency as soon as possible. However, if you look for a way out from fantasy because the problem is urgent, it is "treating silk and making it more chaotic."

Understanding currency from currency is like understanding clouds from clouds and fog, and there is no way to understand it. (Currency in this article, of course, refers to gold and silver or paper money representing gold and silver). Currency is naturally grown and developed from the process of commodity exchange. Commodities and currency exist at the same time and will perish at the same time. If we preserve the commodity economy on the one hand and abandon currency on the other, it is like removing the axles on the one hand and still wanting the wheels to move forward. That is impossible. Currency is an internal development of the commodity economy and is produced by "exchange." We cannot introduce some "certificates" from outside the economy to replace currency. Needless to say, even in terms of gold and silver, obtaining large quantities of gold and silver from outside the economy (such as war booty and reparations) can naturally promote the growth of finance and the development of the economy; but the transformation of gold and silver into currency must also go through "exchange." Because currency is inherently gold and silver, but gold and silver are not originally currency. Therefore, the degree of development of currency depends on the size of the scope and value of commodity exchange.

The reason why currency becomes currency is because it itself is a commodity and has value. Only things that have value in themselves can be used as a measure of all values. More importantly, currency is a social relationship in a commodity society; abolishing currency will hinder and destroy this relationship.

Those who advocate "property certificates," "goods certificates," and similar theories have not noticed that the labor products of individuals cannot become social general labor products, that is, they cannot become exchange value and cannot become currency, before they have been exchanged. In other words, without currency, the products of each individual would either return to barter, or would be unable to circulate. Inability to circulate is of course a declaration of social stagnation, disorder, and disintegration, but barter is by no means acceptable to modern society. Therefore, if the whole country abolishes currency in this way to revolutionize currency, the result will only be to revolutionize one's own life.

These are some important explanations on this point.

So, how should we solve China's currency problem? Where is the basic tone of the solution? To put it simply, the first step is to remove the infringement of the great powers and feudal forces. But the feudal forces are supported by the great powers, so "nine nines return to one." Currently, the most important thing is to break away from the various direct and indirect infringements imposed on us by the great powers. Otherwise, all facilities will be destroyed, will be used, and will cause greater disputes and problems.

Therefore, there is no way to understand currency from currency, and it will be even more impossible to solve the currency problem by solving the currency problem.

(Note 1) Safanov: The Great Development of Chinese Society.

(Note 2) op. cit.

(Note 3) Mr. Zhu Jingzhou's investigation report, see Shen Bao, April 21 and 22, 1935.

The Course of Soviet Monetary Reform 182

— Wu Binglian

Based on the difference in the socialist economic system of the Soviet Union, its monetary policy is also quite different from that of capitalist countries. What should be pointed out first is the credit system, which is sufficient to influence Soviet monetary policy. Its great difference from capitalism lies in the fact that "it can utilize all monetary assets in a planned way... because all Soviet credit institutions are concentrated in the hands of one owner—the Soviet state." Because of this reason, it can "implement a certain policy of distributing these monetary assets, so it can publicly promote the consolidation and development of socialist elements in the Soviet economy." Because the credit system plays a major role in the socialist economic sector, the government must consolidate its central credit institutions and complete its credit system. Thus, the Soviet State Bank, Industrial Bank, Agricultural Bank, Cooperative Bank, Central Construction Bank, National Trade Bank... constitute this credit system, shouldering special tasks in the Soviet economic sector. For this reason, the State Bank is granted the right of paper money issuance (The Right emission), in order to facilitate financial activities and circulation. Therefore, the credit system naturally plays a major role in the Soviet Union's monetary policy.

Pre-Revolutionary Russia was a country with long-term financial disorder, and the credit system was almost completely destroyed. It was not until the mid-19th century that a silver standard was adopted, stabilizing it for some time. From the end of the 19th century to the outbreak of the European War, a gold standard system was implemented, which was relatively stable for a longer period. However, as soon as the war broke out, due to the over-issuance of paper money and the reduction of deposit amounts, the credit system was completely bankrupted again. Even after the establishment of the Soviet policy, the same policy had to be adopted to raise war funds in order to cope with domestic wars and the siege of international imperialism. As a result, paper money flooded the market, and prices soared. On the eve of 1922, the price of the ruble had reached the point where one pre-war ruble was equal to 288,000 paper rubles. At that time, calculations had to be done in "millions." Due to the inconvenience in calculation techniques, the Soviet government had to change the name of the paper currency. As a result, in 1923, a paper currency was issued, one ruble of which was equal to 100 rubles of the paper currency issued in 1921. However, this method of exchanging names also reduced the trouble of calculation but could not completely stop the continuous decline in the value of paper money. As a result, on the one hand, it hindered the correct calculation of commodities and hindered the development of industry and commerce. On the other hand, it also invisibly increased the burden on the working masses of workers and peasants. Therefore, the Soviet government had to urgently solve the phenomenon of paper money flooding the market and implement monetary reform. In October 1921, the government established a new state bank to take on the task of regulating finance; this bank was under the control of the People's Committee of Finance, with a capital of 200 million Soviet rubles, which was equivalent to about 15 million gold rubles at the then market price. In October 1922, the State Bank accepted the government's order and began to issue a new currency called Chiervoniets—that is, ten-ruble gold notes. This new monetary unit served as the foundation for stabilizing the Soviet state's financial disorder, and the New Economic Policy also began to be implemented in this year, which was of great significance in Soviet history.

At that time, 25% of the value of Chiervoniets was guaranteed by gold and stable foreign gold coins, while the remaining 75% was mostly guaranteed by promissory notes or commodities. However, it could not be used to fill the gap in the state budget, so the deficit in the budget still had to be made up for by Soviet paper money, as before. As a result, the value of paper money was still falling at an accelerated pace.

In fact, the complete realization of the monetary reform was after 1924, because on February 5th of this year, the Chiervoniestr was distinguished by: The value of Chiervoniest would not be lower than ten gold rubles at least, and the national currency was lower than ten rubles, with one yuan, three yuan, and five yuan rubles. The national currency was issued by the State Gold Treasury Bureau, while Chiervoniest was issued by the State Bank. Chiervoniest was guaranteed by gold and foreign gold coins, etc., while the national currency had no such guarantees at all. At that time, the method of stabilizing the national currency was: A The state was responsible for circulating the national currency according to the market price of Chiervoniest (that is, one Chiervoniest was equal to ten national currency rubles), so that it could be exchanged with Chiervoniest without any obstacles. B The amount of national currency issued by the state could only be limited to what was necessary for the exchange of Chiervoniest.

At that time, in addition to announcing the order to issue national currency, an order was also issued on the minting and issuance of silver coins and copper coins: silver coins were divided into four types: one ruble, fifty kopecks, twenty kopecks, and ten kopecks; copper coins were divided into four types: five kopecks, three kopecks, two kopecks, and one kopeck. Among the silver coins, those with a value of one ruble and fifty kopecks contained a higher gold value, so they were divided into "high value," while the remaining twenty kopecks and ten kopecks were "low value."

As soon as this new plan was implemented, the issuance of Soviet paper money was immediately stopped, and the Soviet paper money was completely eliminated by exchanging it at the market price of one national currency ruble equal to five million Soviet paper money. The phenomenon of financial disorder no longer existed, and the Soviet economy obtained a solid monetary unit.

Since 1929, the Soviet Union has implemented a bread rationing system, domestic prices have been regulated and cannot be unified, and state-owned stores and consumer cooperatives have emerged. Because the prices of goods sold in state-owned stores and consumer cooperatives are different from those of the working class who have bread ration coupons, their prices are always several times more expensive than general prices. Moreover, state-owned stores must use foreign currency; this system naturally had great significance in consolidating the Soviet economy at that time. Otherwise, the Soviet Union's socialist industrial construction could not have proceeded smoothly. By 1930, Soviet Russia's finances felt difficult, because the practice of the Five-Year Plan and the temporary demands of various organizations required huge amounts of funds to be increased and added to the annual budget and final accounts, so it was necessary to issue public bonds and huge amounts of paper money according to the plan to make up for the deficit. However, the production of commodities must be adapted to it, so as not to destroy the balance between currency and prices. However, industry in this year could not be fully carried out to this extent, and the light industry sector was the first to be in this state in terms of quantity. As a result, the industrial and financial plans were affected, and huge amounts of funds needed to be added. On the other hand, the collective farms and state-owned farms, which broke through the Five-Year Plan and developed rapidly, also needed huge amounts of subsidies. Even so, the State Bank and the People's Committee of Finance had to issue paper money beyond the plan to cope with the situation.

According to the increase rate of the Soviet Union's currency, it is usually 30%, and in the early part of that year (1930), the issuance of Soviet national currency had reached 2.2 billion rubles, the issuance of paper money had reached 3.8 billion rubles, and the issuance of public bonds had reached 2.4 billion rubles; the increase in currency was already very huge. From April to October 1930, it increased to 48.5% according to the normal increase rate, and at the end of the year, it increased to 61%, which was more than double the normal rate. This huge increase immediately shook the stability of the Soviet monetary system. Therefore, the seriousness of this financial difficulty can be imagined.

During this period, the Soviet government, in view of this critical situation, immediately ordered the People's Committee of Finance to stop the issuance of paper money for the large amounts of funds needed by the Grain Preparation Committee, economic construction, cultural construction... in the fourth quarter. The cessation of paper money issuance, in turn, caused the currency to stagnate in the hands of the people, unable to be transferred to the national bank's treasury. At the same time, the low increase rate of light industry also made it impossible to absorb the people's purchasing power, so the State Bank had to stop payments in order to save the shortage of currency.

Thus, due to the volatility of the currency and the emptiness of the national treasury, the Soviet government had to find ways to overcome this difficulty from the objective situation, otherwise the entire economic system would fall into bankruptcy. Therefore, the government immediately seized several characteristics of the time to seriously implement:

(1) Expand the increase in production and promote the movement to increase labor productivity;

(2) Overcome the uneconomical operation, establish an economic clearing system, systematically reduce production costs, strictly pursue profits, and intensify accumulation within the industry

(3) Overcome the lack of strictness in the fiscal plan. And because of this, it is related to the reform of the fiscal plan, tax system, credit system, etc.

This difficulty was completely overcome in early 1931. And the Five-Year Plan broke through these many difficulties and achieved great development. This also explains the significance of the Soviet State Bank's announcement of another monetary reform on December 1, 1935. That is to say, the shift of the monetary system changes with the development of the economy. In the past few years, the Soviet economy has made rapid progress, gradually becoming a self-sufficient country, and the national economy has been improving day by day, so the change of its monetary system is a matter of course.

This monetary reform is adapted to the improvement of the Soviet national economy; it is closely related to the abolition of the bread rationing system, and it also has great significance.

In the past, the establishment of state-owned stores was implemented at the same time as the bread rationing system, mainly to facilitate the purchase of people who did not receive bread ration coupons, which was due to the prevention of food panic. Now that bread rationing has been abolished and the development of the food industry is sufficient to supply it, the state-owned stores will naturally be abolished, which is beyond doubt.

After the abolition of state-owned stores, the prices of goods in the Soviet Union gradually became unified, without the special differences that existed before. At the same time, due to the increase in the value of the ruble, workers' wages have also increased invisibly. On the other hand, the progress of production has also promoted the decline in prices. According to a TASS dispatch on November 9 last year, "In the first nine months of this year, the total wages increased by 23.2% compared with the same period last year, while in the past ten months, the prices of collective farm products fell by 20-25%." At the same time, Havas also telegraphed, "From January next year, retail prices will be suppressed by 15-40%, and wages will also be reduced, but the reduction rate will not be as great as the reduction in the prices of manufactured goods and food; in other words, although wages appear to be reduced on the surface, actual wages will increase instead." From this, we can see how much the improvement of the lives of Soviet workers and peasants has reached.

Due to the reason for abolishing state-owned stores, the method of paying in foreign currency for the money remitted to Soviet residents from abroad has also been abolished, and it is completely paid in Soviet legal tender. Therefore, the government stipulated that its market price was 1.333 francs per 100 rubles, but it will not apply until January 1 this year, and it will be raised to a price of three francs per ruble. Foreign exchange has also changed because of this. In the past, the exchange rate was about 13 francs and 60 centimes per ruble, but foreigners were unwilling to exchange rubles at this market price because state-owned stores exercised foreign currency. In fact, the purchasing power of the ruble was less than half a franc in the past, but after it was set as half a franc, the living standard of foreigners could not help but increase. However, now that the prices in the Soviet Union are still falling continuously, the purchasing power of the ruble will also increase accordingly, and the lives of foreigners will not suffer because of this.

Since this monetary system was reformed again, the Soviet Union's international exchange will undoubtedly be more stable, which is of greater significance to the Soviet Union's foreign trade. In today's international currency war, which is becoming increasingly acute, it is not without significance to trace the progress of the Soviet Union's monetary system and its role in economic construction.

Extra Edition of Shen Bao Local News

Discourse

Abolishing Petty Gratuities 202

— Meng Ruo

"Petty gratuities" are a bad custom that needs to be abolished. In various places in China, hotels, teahouses, restaurants, bathhouses, theaters, barber shops, and other entertainment venues all have the practice of charging petty gratuities. This is a widespread practice in various industries and has become a customary rule. Restaurants openly hang up signs that say "Patrons are requested to add a gratuity." Not only that, what is even more unreasonable is that in addition to the petty gratuity, the waiter or attendant also demands a tip for the drinks? This counts as an extra petty gratuity. Moreover, the amount of the petty gratuity is fixed, while the extra petty gratuity is not. Therefore, waiters and attendants often arbitrarily demand them. This is not only inconvenient for customers, but also has a significant impact on the business of various industries.

The New Life Movement General Association, in view of this, believes that the collection of petty gratuities by various industries violates the spirit of the New Life Movement, and has formulated "Implementation Measures for Eliminating Extra Petty Gratuities" and distributed them to New Life Movement associations throughout the country for promotion in order to abolish this bad custom.

However, it must be noted here that the bad custom of collecting petty gratuities is closely related to the waiter system. In hotels and restaurants throughout China, the wages of employed waiters and employees are very low, or even non-existent, and they rely on petty gratuities as compensation. This is naturally a good deal for the operators, who have customers pay to hire employees. The waiters and employees also do not work for free, and those with high skills sometimes earn more from petty gratuities than from ordinary wages. This is also the origin of the forced demand for drink money. Therefore, we believe that to eliminate petty gratuities, we must fundamentally improve the waiter system in various industries, which is convenient for guests. This is the best example.

Recently, some entertainment venues in this city have voluntarily abolished petty gratuities, which will definitely be very beneficial to their business. We hope that various industries can follow suit and abolish the bad custom of petty gratuities. This may be an effective way to revitalize business.

Mosquito Incense 203

— Li Yinfei

Pushing open the window, in front of me is a large meadow.

This meadow was originally a wasteland. When I moved here, it was barren. Now it is covered with lush fragrant grass. In the evening, groups of children come here to play soccer, using it as a soccer field. At night, it becomes the headquarters of mosquitoes, buzzing around everywhere.

I have been thinking about installing a screen window to keep out the mosquitoes and block the wind, but I always put it off because I can't afford it. If I close the window, there are fewer mosquitoes, but it's unbearable hot. If I don't close it, there is wind, but also swarms of mosquitoes, bumping into people's legs and buzzing incessantly in people's ears, making it impossible to read a book or write a few words.

Therefore, I have to resort to mosquito incense, hoping to use its power to get some peace and quiet. Isn't this a good time to read a little or write something in this pleasant breeze?

The mosquito incense is lit. I even prepared an incense cage for it. Looking at the light blue smoke rising up, I have the lighthearted feeling of an old poet. I feel that it is worth it to light a coil of mosquito incense just to add a little so-called "poetic flavor." At the same time, those lines of poetry like "leaning against the incense burner until dawn" and "a red sleeve adds fragrance" also come to mind.

Enjoying the cool breeze, like a new moon hanging in the clouds, watching the light blue smoke rising, and listening to the intermittent insect sounds on the grass, the voices of the people chatting in the shade under the wall also seem blurred. This is a poetic realm.

But this poetic realm is immediately pulled back by reality. The mosquitoes are no longer buzzing in my ears, they are all concentrated under the desk, bumping and flying around on my legs, making my legs itch and swell up again.

I rub the itchy spots with flower dew, and then light another coil of mosquito incense under the desk. This time, I lit the lighter with a triumphant and contemptuous smile. My heart also gently leaped and said: "I have a better weapon than you, let's see how you deal with me!"

In this way, I persisted for several nights, and the mosquitoes could only hide in the dark corners, flapping their weak wings.

Sometimes, I heard the people under the wall chasing away mosquitoes with fans, and a triumphant glow appeared on my face. I praised myself for being clever, and felt that those who used fans to chase mosquitoes were really too stupid.

One day, I received a letter from a friend in a distant place. The letter reported the farmers' resistance to taxes in that area, saying that the farmers were resisting taxes because they could not afford them, and the military and police used force to suppress them, resulting in a conflict. My passionate friend, having witnessed such a tragedy, expressed his grievances with pen and ink.

That night, I planned to write a reply to him, advising him to be more rational and not so passionate. Especially in the interior, being overly passionate sometimes only harms oneself and does not help others. But when I sat at my desk, habitually preparing to light the mosquito incense, I found that there was only one coil of mosquito incense left. I rummaged through the drawers, and there were only a few copper coins scattered in them. After a brief consideration, I felt that "poetic flavor" was ultimately not as important as practicality, so I decided to put it under the desk.

I had written half of the letter when I fell into contemplation. I did not believe that I could persuade him. A young man with flesh and blood and emotions, living in a historical tragedy, cannot stand by and watch with detached neutrality.

I was troubled by this problem, and my pen stopped writing. The mosquito incense shrunk circle by circle, and finally went out. I hungrily stared at it, and finally found an answer on it. At that time, hungry mosquitoes surrounded me again, and probably because of hunger, they were especially fierce.

I tore up the written letter, and in the mosquito attack, I told him about my experience with mosquito incense. That's all! I didn't say anything else.

Hypocrisy 204

— Xue Ye

——Travel Notes, Part Two

Because I am used to living in the city, all my living habits have unknowingly become modern. So when I ran into this ancient city, which was half-revealing the appearance of modern civilization and half-dragging the tail of the feudal era, I felt that everything was fresh, and what appeared in my eyes was the shadow of the old society that had been forgotten.

Before starting the journey, I knew that this ancient city had a kind of inviolable dignity, because it is an area where the inherent Chinese morality is practiced. People who are used to living in the city may forget our inherent morality and offend this solemn holy place. So, when I arrived here, I paid special attention to all the forms, wanting to find the dignity and morality that I wanted to know here.

A friend told me that you will not see the enchanting prostitutes in this ancient city, you will not find the blacklisted compatriots, you will not hear the sound of bamboo cards, and you will not be able to buy the smuggled inferior goods. In short, what you see is solemnity and cleanliness. At first, I trusted my friend's words, because this is an ancient city that practices inherent morality. But after a rainy day, the dream was overturned by the facts, and I began to doubt this ancient city.

Page 18

It was the second day I was here. I was walking on the road in the commercial district, and various goods flashed before my eyes. Among the goods, inferior goods often flew into my eyes, which made me pay more attention to distinguishing them. Because I used to be a businessman myself, I still have full confidence in my knowledge of goods. From that time on, the belief in the ancient city in my heart began to waver.

In order to deceive myself, I still thought it was a treacherous merchant's trick, but the things that were jumping in front of my eyes happened one by one. The already wavering belief finally fell into the abyss of destruction.

——Although the enchanting prostitutes did not hang up signs, but from the lively places of the public, they were full of gloomy demon spirit, and the newspapers also had lewd descriptions or reports.

——Although it is clearly stated that those who receive salaries should abide by the law, the clapping sound that scatters in the night sky every night flows out from the homes of those who receive salaries. Knowing the law and breaking the law has ancient precedents.

——The rest, all the morality that cannot be exhausted is destroyed. The solemnity and cleanliness that my friend said are stained in reality.

Chinese people love hypocrisy. In our daily life, the shadow of hypocrisy is everywhere. However, when it comes into contact with reality, the hypocrisy reveals a distressing ugliness.

After spending three full days of solemn life in the hypocritical ancient city, I finally set foot on the journey and walked out of the holy land of the ancient city on a hot afternoon, looking up at the vast wilderness. The depressed heart for a few days seemed to have been liberated and was extraordinarily comfortable.

In Memory 205

— Lin Na

It's raining, and the night sky is completely shrouded in deep darkness.

Under the feeble light of fifteen lamps, I anxiously flipped through the pages of a book, thinking, "Perhaps I can find something inside!" However, no! I found nothing, as if I couldn't find the reason for my depression. So, my burning eyes desperately turned away from the pages and gazed at the heavy, dark sky.

In the sky, a dense web of fine rain pillars filled the air, and the night shook with its enormous, clumsy body.

Darkness, darkness, just darkness! I stood up from my chair, feeling stifled, and started pacing gently around the house.

Suddenly, I felt a thought ripple through my mind, then slowly expand into a vivid, real image. It was a face, a familiar pale face, it was Hua! I whispered to myself, a nervous, petite, and easily sentimental girl. On this day last year, I met her in Ming's place. At that time, she was still a lively, talkative girl; but later, she changed, completely changed, becoming so dull and melancholy. Sometimes she would come to my place and gently knock on the door, but when I rushed out to open it and invited her in, she would stare at me blankly with her lost eyes for a while, then sadly murmur in a trembling voice:

"No! I can't go in, they can't help me, this dull life!" Then she silently lifted her foot, turned, and left. This startled me so much that I followed closely behind her until she disappeared under the street lamp outside the alley, then I reluctantly turned back. However, I didn't forget the words she said in an excited tone: "No! I can't go on like this, I definitely can't… can't," yes, she can't go on like this! And I sighed.

However, at this moment, my ears were constantly vibrated, as if a low, trembling voice was calling out: "No! I can't go on like this, I definitely can't…" I lowered my head in sorrow, and an unusual impulse made me grab the only old coat from the rack, put on my hat, and open the door to go out. From afar, I could still hear that trembling voice…

The street was calm and quiet, the oily road surface already wet, gently glistening under the intense light.

I walked, heedlessly. On this silent street, I couldn't hear any unusual sounds, I couldn't see any unusual shadows. All there was, was myself, the monotonous footsteps, accompanied by a lonely shadow.

At the corner, I suddenly stopped abruptly. A latent thought was so actively running through my mind, reminding me of what had happened two months ago. Wasn't Hua missing two months ago? Why am I looking for her now? In her small, cramped room, it should be gloomy now; the light, that bright light, might be disappearing in front of the wide window. My heart trembled uneasily, and my footsteps continued moving unnaturally, into the unknowable darkness. …………

The area was becoming increasingly deserted. First, the main street disappeared at the corner, and then the lights were gone. At this moment, everything was gone. Darkness, accompanied by fine raindrops, slanted onto people's faces; however, I didn't feel it was chilling, no! My heart was confused and fiery.

Suddenly I felt my whole body turn cold, and when I regained consciousness, I realized that I was completely immersed in the dense rain. Here, the surroundings were vast, and darkness overflowed.

Starting Work 206

— Ai Cha

Half a month later, Old Chen and Old Qian frowned as they did the accounting:

"Hey! Little Li! Come here! See if there are any mistakes!"

"It must be a loss, what's the point of calculating!"

After half a day, they finally finished the accounts, reluctantly.

"My god! We still lost more than ten yuan!"

They sighed, the salary of tens of dollars vanished like a bubble.

(Note 1: One dot of paper is one cent.)

(Note 2: Running the horse means working as a laborer.)

(Note 3: 起版 (qi ban) means completed.)

United Publishing House Establishes Publishing Department 213

It is heard that the United Publishing House is currently expanding, bringing authors and readers together to achieve their ideal publishing business, establishing a publishing department, and recruiting members.
